and whose reproductive health clinics closed due to TRAP laws already can't access birth control. And as a logical thinker and data and science appreciator, @sullydish should know that when people can't access birth control, they then need - surprise - abortions!

or their religions to tell them how to vote. We would put the health and safety of ~150 million American women into our current toxic mix of propaganda, voter suppression, Super PAC corruption, and religious-theocratic voter manipulation campaigns? That would be dangerous.
My Prop 8 experience in CA shows us on an issue that @sullydish cares about how referendums to grant or deny people's fundamental rights can easily go wrong. Legislatures are gerrymandered. People can't vote. Some people won't vote. And others are manipulated by special interests
Roe gave us safe and legal abortion. It saves lives. 25-33% of all women will have an abortion. Women are half the population. Almost 4 billion people on this planet are women. And @sullydish wants to condescend to us that why can't we have a referendum on our rights?
I have no vested interest in Obergefell other than my joy in knowing that it helps others and gives us a society based in equality that we want as Americans and as humans on this tiny blue dot.
I, too, relied on the courts to save us to overturn Prop 8. I cried tears of joy and relief when Obergefell was decided. In law school, I spoke up against the bigots when it was discussed in our community property class. I pointed out the beautiful language of Kennedy's decision.
When @sullydish's issue was in the news during my young adulthood, I immediately saw how I could help - by teaching my son that everyone is valuable, by championing equality, by voting, by boycotting stores that supported the opposing position on CA's marriage referendum in 2008.
Just like NOW. I'm not gay. I knew no gay people growing up. I was raised Catholic &amp; was told gay people were bad &amp; I should tell them to not be gay so they wouldn't go to hell. I met a few gay women at hockey during high school.
My friend had an abortion in the 1960s when she was 13. Her family had to scrape together $1000. In the 1960s when average family income was what? $5k/year? There was a groundswell that the recent anti-abortion laws were wrong and needed to be changed.
Husbands who lost wives in botched abortions wanted other women to be able to access them safely. Parents who lost daughters did the same. (See more recently, Savita's family in Ireland who helped change their laws.)
The courts and the legislature follow public opinion. By 1973, there was an outcry from women and their allies - not just our natural allies against the patriarchy, gay men - but straight men who didn't want the state to force them to be parents every time they had sex!
If their wives health wouldn't allow them to have any more kids, the Founding Fathers could easily access prostitutes. So of course they didn't think about midwives and abortions and women's rights. They weren't on their radar. And not just because radar didn't exist yet.
Of course the Founders didn't think about marriage equality. Of course they didn't think about abortion. They could easily replace a wife who died in childbirth with another woman. They could easily create more slaves by impregnating their own slaves. https://t.co/dtx11nz6ZA
of the expansion of our rights - not directly spelled out in the Constitution, but that our understanding of evolved over time.
The Court could see that anti-abortion laws were fairly recent, did nothing to prevent abortions, and led poor women to unsafe methods that put their lives and health in danger. Even now, 70% of Americans favor abortion rights. Like marriage equality, it was a natural progression https://t.co/R7niWm47Tz
To say that Roe was passed by an "activist court" without public support denies reality. That activist court also gave us Mapp v Ohio. Miranda v AZ. Gideon v Wainwright. Griswold v CT. What Earl Warren started flowed through to Roe because the courts looked at the data.
Courts were the only resort of gay couples to validate their marriages because of the hodgepodge of friendly laws to other states who had extremely hateful laws passed by people who were whipped up into anti-gay prejudice by special interest groups with a lot of money.
